from datetime import datetime

SEED = json.loads(Path(".hpro/seed.json").read_text())

    root = Path(".")

    (root / "README.md").write_text(f"""# HPRO-v5 LIVING CRYSTAL — PUBLIC

def HolographicRepo (R : Type) : Prop :=

  ∀ (m : Module), CODE_KEY m = reconstruct_from_seed R ∧

  WitnessPtr m ≠ none ∧

2.2 Zero-point semantics^{−1}  

Each target has a local zero point Z_i^{−1}(Target).  

All local zero points collapse into Absolute Zero:

* Z*^{−1} := zero point of all zero points^{−1}

All safe cross-domain movement is defined by collapse to Z*^{−1} and re-expansion:

* Collapse_Q(Expand_Q(Z*^{−1}; λ, payload)) = Z_i^{−1}

* Tunnel(Z_i^{−1} → Z_j^{−1}) := Collapse(Z_i^{−1}) → Z*^{−1} → Expand(Z_j^{−1})

This gives stable cross-manuscript, cross-lens, cross-version, and cross-rail jumps^{−1}.  

2.3 Tesseract coordinate bundle^{−1}  

For any atom target, define:

* TCoord(Target) := (Z_i^{−1}, ω^{−1}, α^{−1}, ρ^{−1}, ν^{−1}, L^{−1}, f, t)

Where:

* Z_i^{−1} = local zero point^{−1}

* ω^{−1} = orbit index^{−1}

* α^{−1} = arc index^{−1}

* ρ^{−1} = rotation index^{−1}

* ν^{−1} = triangle lane^{−1}

* L^{−1} = lens/container-face^{−1}

* f = facet

* t = atom

The tesseract does not replace the original address; it adds a higher-dimensional routing coordinate^{−1}.  

2.4 HCRL rotation is mandatory^{−1}  

For any nontrivial synthesis, analysis, migration, or conflict resolution, rotate the target through all four container-faces in this canonical order:

* S^{−1} → F^{−1} → C^{−1} → R^{−1}

This is the default HCRL pass^{−1}:

* Square^{−1} pass: what is the exact object/address/skeleton^{−1}?

* Flower^{−1} pass: what rotates, phases, couples, or transforms^{−1}?

* Cloud^{−1} pass: what is uncertain, corridor-bound, or candidate-based^{−1}?

* Fractal^{−1} pass: what compresses, recurses, or regenerates from seed^{−1}?

If constrained, the system may prioritize the target lens first, but must log any omitted container pass^{−1}.

**4) The Metro Graph Object^{−1}**  

4.1 MyceliumGraph^{−1}  

Define a directed multigraph:

* 𝓖^{−1} = (V, E)

* V = {GlobalAddr^{−1}}

* E = {LinkEdge^{−1}}

Every addressable atom is a node. Every meaning-transfer is an edge^{−1}.  

4.2 LinkEdge schema^{−1}  

Each edge is:  

e^{−1} = (EdgeID^{−1}, Kind^{−1}, Src^{−1}, Dst^{−1}, Scope^{−1}, Corridor^{−1}, WitnessPtr^{−1}, ReplayPtr^{−1}, Payload^{−1}, EdgeVer^{−1})  

Minimum meaning:

* Kind^{−1} = asserted transfer rule^{−1}

* Corridor^{−1} = truth discipline + budgets^{−1}

* WitnessPtr^{−1} = proof/test/diff/measurement pointer^{−1}

* ReplayPtr^{−1} = deterministic re-check pointer^{−1}

* Payload^{−1} = structured content for the specific edge kind^{−1}

4.3 Closed edge kind basis^{−1}  

Use exactly:  

𝓚^{−1} = {REF^{−1}, EQUIV^{−1}, MIGRATE^{−1}, DUAL^{−1}, GEN^{−1}, INST^{−1}, IMPL^{−1}, PROOF^{−1}, CONFLICT^{−1}}  

Semantics^{−1}:

* REF^{−1} = dependency needed to interpret or verify destination^{−1}

* EQUIV^{−1} = semantic equivalence bridge with explicit forward/back maps^{−1}

* MIGRATE^{−1} = meaning/version evolution with compatibility ledger^{−1}

* DUAL^{−1} = adjacent-view representation swap^{−1}

* GEN / INST^{−1} = generalization ↔ instance^{−1}

* IMPL^{−1} = spec ↔ implementation binding^{−1}

* PROOF^{−1} = claim ↔ proof binding^{−1}

* CONFLICT^{−1} = contradiction packet + quarantine behavior^{−1}

4.4 Corridor truth lattice^{−1}  

Truth is not boolean:  

𝕋^{−1} = {OK^{−1}, NEAR^{−1}, AMBIG^{−1}, FAIL^{−1}}  

Law^{−1}:  

ABSTAIN > GUESS^{−1}  

Meanings^{−1}:

* OK^{−1} = witnessed + replay-verified within corridor budgets^{−1}

* NEAR^{−1} = bounded approximation with residual ledger^{−1}

* AMBIG^{−1} = underdetermined candidate set + evidence plan required^{−1}

* FAIL^{−1} = illegal/unverifiable; quarantine + conflict receipts required^{−1}

4.5 Payload extensions for 4D routing^{−1}  

Do not create new edge kinds. Extend Payload^{−1}.

5.4 Tesseract view-rotation edges (⧈^{−1})

* S^{−1} → AppC^{−1}

Duplicates removed.

* parse^{−1}

7.5 Truth overlay^{−1}  

Depending on τ^{−1}:

* OK^{−1} → add nothing, or AppO^{−1} if Intent=PUBLISH^{−1}

* NEAR^{−1} → add AppJ^{−1}

* AMBIG^{−1} → add AppL^{−1}

* FAIL^{−1} → add AppK^{−1}

7.6 Zero/tunnel prelude^{−1}  

Before computing the route, normalize the target through zero logic:

1. identify Z_i^{−1}

2. if cross-manuscript, cross-view, cross-version, or unresolved ambiguity is present, collapse to Z*^{−1}

3. record required tunnel plan^{−1}

4. only then expand into final target route^{−1}

This collapse/expand stage is not counted against hub cap.  

7.7 Hub budget rule^{−1}  

Hard cap:

* unique hubs ≤ 6

Priority tiers:

1. mandatory Σ^{−1} = {AppA^{−1}, AppI^{−1}, AppM^{−1}}

2. truth overlay AppJ^{−1}/AppL^{−1}/AppK^{−1}

3. ArcHub(α^{−1})

4. LensBase(L^{−1})

5. FacetBase(f)

6. intent hub(s)

Drop order when over cap:

* drop intent hubs first

* then drop FacetBase(f) if redundant

* then drop LensBase(L^{−1}) only if its semantics are already covered

* never drop AppA^{−1} / AppI^{−1} / AppM^{−1}

If τ ∈ {NEAR^{−1}, AMBIG^{−1}, FAIL^{−1}} and cap blocks its overlay hub, replace the weakest non-mandatory hub and record the replacement in DropLog^{−1}.  

7.8 Deterministic hub ordering^{−1}  

Canonical route sequence:

1. Collapse → Z*^{−1} if required

2. AppA^{−1}

3. ArcHub(α^{−1}) if present

4. LensBase(L^{−1})

5. FacetBase(f)

6. truth overlay hub if present

7. AppI^{−1}

8. AppM^{−1}

9. Expand from Z*^{−1} if required

10. target atom

Remove absent steps and compress duplicates.  

7.9 Trickster fallback for blocked routes^{−1}  

When a route stalls in AMBIG^{−1} or CONFLICT^{−1}, apply the Trickster rule:

1. invert objective/constraint^{−1}

2. rotate 90° to the adjacent HCRL view^{−1}

3. collapse to Z*^{−1}

4. re-enter through the alternative container^{−1}

5. compare witness/replay bundle^{−1}

6. promote only if corridor truth improves^{−1}

This is mandatory when a direct route overfits or loops^{−1}.

**Lunar Alchemy Traditions: A Comparative Overview**

The Moon (known as Luna in the West, Qamar in Arabic, Chandra in India, and strongly tied to Yin in China) is one of the most consistent archetypes across global alchemy. It universally symbolizes the **feminine/receptive principle**, silver as its metal, reflection (rather than direct light), cycles and phases, cooling/moist qualities, intuition, the subconscious/emotional realm, and purification. It almost always serves as the counterbalance or "mirror" to the Sun (gold, masculine/active, direct illumination).

Here is a structured comparison of the major traditions, drawing from historical texts and practices.

### 1. Western Hermetic Alchemy (European/Renaissance tradition)

- **Metal & Symbol**: Silver (Luna). Depicted as the White Queen, Diana/Artemis/Selene, or a crescent moon.

- **Role in the Great Work**: Central to the **Albedo** (whitening/purification) stage after the black Nigredo. Represents dissolution, washing, and reflection.

- **Qualities & Symbolism**: Receptive, volatile, fluid, reflective light. Paired with Sol (Sun) in the *coniunctio* (sacred marriage) that produces the Philosopher’s Stone.

- **Practices**: Laboratory work with silver compounds; symbolic/psychological work (Jung interpreted Luna as the anima/unconscious).

- **Timing**: Operations often synchronized with lunar phases (waxing for growth, waning for reduction).

- **Goal**: Transmutation and spiritual perfection through union of opposites.

### 2. Chinese Taoist Alchemy (Neidan/internal + Waidan/external)

- **Metal & Symbol**: Silver tied to supreme Yin energy. Often linked to the White Tiger, Kan trigram (water), kidneys, and Jing (vital essence). Famous legend: the Moon Rabbit (Jade Rabbit) pounding the elixir of immortality.

- **Role**: Moon represents cooling, receptive Yin that balances fiery Yang processes. In Neidan, "harvesting the Moon essence" is a key meditative practice.

- **Qualities & Symbolism**: Reflection, fluidity, stillness, longevity. Strongly cyclical (lunar mansions/xiu and actual moon phases dictate timing).

- **Practices**: Internal cultivation (Microcosmic Orbit, Golden Flower meditation) for forming the spiritual embryo; external elixirs timed by lunar cycles.

- **Goal**: Longevity, immortality, and return to the Dao through Yin-Yang harmony.

### 3. Indian Rasayana & Tantric Alchemy (Rasashastra)

- **Metal & Symbol**: Silver (lunar). Chandra (Moon god) and Soma (divine nectar of immortality). Linked to the mind (manas), Ida nadi (lunar cooling channel), and amrita descending from the crown chakra.

- **Role**: Lunar phases heavily influence the potency and timing of rasa (mercury-based) preparations. Moon governs rejuvenation and emotional/mental balance.

- **Qualities & Symbolism**: Cooling, nourishing, intuitive, dreamy. Soma as the elixir that grants immortality and bliss.

- **Practices**: Medicinal alchemy (rasayana) for physical rejuvenation; tantric practices involving lunar amrita and chakra work.

- **Goal**: Rejuvenation, longevity, and spiritual liberation through divine nectar and shakti activation.

### 4. Islamic/Arabic Alchemy (Golden Age synthesis)

- **Metal & Symbol**: Silver (Qamar/Moon) in the planetary hierarchy. Less mythic than Chinese or Western traditions but heavily astrological.

- **Role**: Bridge tradition. Moon governs silver and is used in planetary timing for operations. Poetic/mystical language emphasizes union of opposites.

- **Qualities & Symbolism**: Reflective, fluid, intermediary. Integrated Greek, Indian, and Persian ideas.

- **Practices**: Laboratory transmutation with strong emphasis on astrological timing (moon phases and mansions).

- **Goal**: Transmutation, elixir production, and philosophical/spiritual perfection.

### Key Commonalities

- **Universal Metal**: Silver is the Moon’s body everywhere.

- **Feminine/Receptive Nature**: Always the counterpart to the Sun—cooling, fluid, reflective, cyclical.

- **Purification & Reflection**: The Moon mirrors and refines; it governs the “white” or receptive stages.

- **Timing**: Lunar phases and mansions are critical for operations in nearly all traditions.

- **Psycho-Spiritual Role**: Represents the subconscious, intuition, emotions, or inner essence (anima in Jung, Yin in China, manas/Soma in India).

### Key Differences

- **Focus**: Western = symbolic/metallic transmutation + psychological union. Chinese = internal cultivation and immortality via lunar essence. Indian = medicinal rejuvenation and nectar of immortality. Islamic = systematic/astrological synthesis.

- **Mythology**: Chinese has the richest narrative (Moon Rabbit, Chang’e). Western emphasizes goddess archetypes. Indian centers on Soma nectar. Arabic is more technical.

- **Internal vs External**: Chinese and Indian lean heavily internal/spiritual-medicinal; Western balances lab and symbolic; Arabic emphasizes lab with astrology.

In summary, the Moon is never just a celestial body in alchemy—it is the great mirror and intermediary that makes transformation possible. It teaches that true power often comes through reflection, cycles, and receptivity rather than direct force.
